<div id="review_3363557276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3363557276" />
    <a title="Shaitarn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51054342-shaitarn"><img alt="Shaitarn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518449594p2/51054342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3363557276?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaitarn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaitarn" href="/user/show/51054342-shaitarn">Shaitarn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3363557276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10737958173290468893">It was okay. The story had an appropriately huge climax, but I can't help thinking it hasn't aged well. <br/><br/>Feist is a competent writer, but I found part of the story dragging and hard to be very interested in - notably Pug and Tomas' adventures in time and space. As well as finding the whole premise rather ridiculous I felt both characters were absurdly over-powered <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[notably Pug's bending time back to the beginning of the universe <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I can understand it was important for</span>
  <span id="freeText10737958173290468893" style="display:none">It was okay. The story had an appropriately huge climax, but I can't help thinking it hasn't aged well. <br /><br />Feist is a competent writer, but I found part of the story dragging and hard to be very interested in - notably Pug and Tomas' adventures in time and space. As well as finding the whole premise rather ridiculous I felt both characters were absurdly over-powered <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[notably Pug's bending time back to the beginning of the universe <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I can understand it was important for the climax, but the whole thing made me roll my eyes every time the story switched back to them - I found the questing/besieging part of the story far more interesting. It's just a personal preference, and I'm sure some people loved the sections I didn't.<br /><br />Read if you like or are curious about old fashioned fantasy. If you only read modern fantasy and like fast-moving plots with plenty of action, then possibly this won't suit you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10737958173290468893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UfHmSDCyjSdtqqtKJdjNrJyOGzB28xhYXgEsa5BEzgcEl2iiPH/eSclKeQbbPaF16HVCIiGKtoRJ79gsiaIN0g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bc8assTIlEpbZnxXRMjhdt7y4l0kJollNUxw+02BFKo4qZRYyAXHJP+Grhu6LY2vqgm7T3NfJ7kiooS8VGfXfw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1328456724560756717">Raymond E. Feist was born Raymond E. Gonzales III, but took his adoptive step-father's surname when his mother remarried Felix E. Feist. He graduated with a B.A. in Communication Arts with Honors in 1977 from the University of California at San Diego. During that year Feist had some ideas for a novel about a boy who would be a magician. He wrote the novel two years later, and it was published in 1</span>
  <span id="freeText1328456724560756717" style="display:none">Raymond E. Feist was born Raymond E. Gonzales III, but took his adoptive step-father's surname when his mother remarried Felix E. Feist. He graduated with a B.A. in Communication Arts with Honors in 1977 from the University of California at San Diego. During that year Feist had some ideas for a novel about a boy who would be a magician. He wrote the novel two years later, and it was published in 1982 by Doubleday. Feist currently lives in San Diego with his children, where he collects fine wine, DVDs, and books on a variety of topics of personal interest: wine, biographies, history, and, especially, the history of American Professional Football.</span>
